### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-11-07T22:09:30Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1094** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-11-07T22:09:30Z
```diff
@@ -904,29 +902,180 @@ type TopologyDomainAssignment struct {
 }
 ```
 
-Kueue uses the `kueue.x-k8s.io/topology` scheduling gate to delay the
-`nodeSelector` assignment, because different pods in the same PodSet may have
-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+}
+
+type TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues struct {
+  // commonPrefix specifies a common prefix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonPrefix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+  // commonSuffix specifies a common suffix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonSuffix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // roots specifies the values in this assignment, excluding commonPrefix and commonSuffix, if non-empty.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field of the TopologyAssignmentSlice.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Roots []string
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the topology assignment value (on the current topology level)
+  // that applies to every domain in the current slice.
+  // Mutually exclusive with roots, commonPrefix and commonSuffix.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalValue *string
+}
 ```
 
+The above mentioned cross-validity rules (mutually exclusive fields, equal lengths, etc.) will be all expressed as `kubebuilder:validation:XValidation` rules on the respective "smallest common container types".
+
+Example (representing the same assignment as in the first example for the [old format](#until-v1beta1)):
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  slices:
+  - size: 2
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - universalValue: block-1
+    - commonPrefix: rack-
+      roots: [1, 2]
+    counts: [4, 2]
+```
+
+The above example has one slice, specifying 2 domains on 2 topology levels. On the block level, all domains take the same value (`block-1`), which allows using `universalValue`. On the rack level, the values diverge (`rack-1`) vs. (`rack-2`) but they still share a relatively long common prefix. The new representation allows deduplicating characters between these.
+
+Multiple slices may be used e.g. for a host-level assignment when the nodes being assigned are split into multiple "node pools". The following example illustrates this for an assignment of 12 pods on 12 nodes (1 per 1), where the nodes come from 2 pools (of size 5 and 7 respectively), with node names looking like `pool-X-node-Y`:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels: [kubernetes.io/hostname]
+  slices:
+  - size: 5
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-1-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
+    universalCount: 1
+  - size: 7
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-2-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7]
+    universalCount: 1
+```
+
+The main motivation behind the new format is the etcd size limit of 1.5MiB per single resource, which currently restricts the number of nodes that can participate in the assignment for a single workload. (For the v1beta1 format, and the real-life node naming schemes of main K8s vendors, the limit is around 20-30k). The new format helps addressing this problem in 2 time perspectives:
+
+- In the short term, it increases the number of nodes which can fit into 1 etcd entry.
+
+  - By just using a single slice, with extracting common prefix and suffix of all node names, our simulations (for some real-life node naming schemes) suggested a limit of around 60k nodes.
```

  Thank you for clarifying that.
  Indeed, I discussed this in the recent WG Batch community meeting, and I understand that the proposed Topology assignment is still helpful for larger clusters regardless of introducing a separate slice CustomResource.
  
  Currently, AWS EKS supports up to 100K nodes for a single cluster. So, we probably want to introduce a separate Slice object in the near future. But, for sure, we can consider that different from this KEP.

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2025-11-07T22:11:50Z

-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+}
+
+type TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues struct {
+  // commonPrefix specifies a common prefix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonPrefix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+  // commonSuffix specifies a common suffix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonSuffix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // roots specifies the values in this assignment, excluding commonPrefix and commonSuffix, if non-empty.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field of the TopologyAssignmentSlice.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Roots []string
```

  > So, could you add JSON field name and tag? It looks like some new fields do not have those, yet.
  
  JSON field names are already set everywhere, AFAICS.
  
  I now added `omitempty` to 4 fields. (That's tricky for me: these fields are never going to be empty - per our validation rules - so intuitively I expected `omitempty` to make no sense for them; however, I already saw in #7544 that some auto-check forced me to add the tag, still).

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2025-11-07T22:28:38Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1094** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-11-07T22:28:38Z

 }
 ```
 
-Kueue uses the `kueue.x-k8s.io/topology` scheduling gate to delay the
-`nodeSelector` assignment, because different pods in the same PodSet may have
-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+}
+
+type TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues struct {
+  // commonPrefix specifies a common prefix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonPrefix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+  // commonSuffix specifies a common suffix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonSuffix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // roots specifies the values in this assignment, excluding commonPrefix and commonSuffix, if non-empty.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field of the TopologyAssignmentSlice.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Roots []string
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the topology assignment value (on the current topology level)
+  // that applies to every domain in the current slice.
+  // Mutually exclusive with roots, commonPrefix and commonSuffix.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalValue *string
+}
 ```
 
+The above mentioned cross-validity rules (mutually exclusive fields, equal lengths, etc.) will be all expressed as `kubebuilder:validation:XValidation` rules on the respective "smallest common container types".
+
+Example (representing the same assignment as in the first example for the [old format](#until-v1beta1)):
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  slices:
+  - size: 2
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - universalValue: block-1
+    - commonPrefix: rack-
+      roots: [1, 2]
+    counts: [4, 2]
+```
+
+The above example has one slice, specifying 2 domains on 2 topology levels. On the block level, all domains take the same value (`block-1`), which allows using `universalValue`. On the rack level, the values diverge (`rack-1`) vs. (`rack-2`) but they still share a relatively long common prefix. The new representation allows deduplicating characters between these.
+
+Multiple slices may be used e.g. for a host-level assignment when the nodes being assigned are split into multiple "node pools". The following example illustrates this for an assignment of 12 pods on 12 nodes (1 per 1), where the nodes come from 2 pools (of size 5 and 7 respectively), with node names looking like `pool-X-node-Y`:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels: [kubernetes.io/hostname]
+  slices:
+  - size: 5
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-1-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
+    universalCount: 1
+  - size: 7
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-2-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7]
+    universalCount: 1
+```
+
+The main motivation behind the new format is the etcd size limit of 1.5MiB per single resource, which currently restricts the number of nodes that can participate in the assignment for a single workload. (For the v1beta1 format, and the real-life node naming schemes of main K8s vendors, the limit is around 20-30k). The new format helps addressing this problem in 2 time perspectives:
+
+- In the short term, it increases the number of nodes which can fit into 1 etcd entry.
+
+  - By just using a single slice, with extracting common prefix and suffix of all node names, our simulations (for some real-life node naming schemes) suggested a limit of around 60k nodes.
```

  OK, let me take this opportunity to discuss for the future :)
  
  My rough experiments suggest that even 100K (in particular, for AWS naming) may be fittable without a CRD, if we play with multiple Slices in a "prefix-suffix-smart" way. 
  (By which I mean: organize nodes into Slices so that Slices have long common prefixes, etc.).
  
  Though here, (as already mentioned in this KEP), there is a tradeoff between 3 factors:
  1. High node limit
  2. Good time performance of the "encoding"
  3. Conceptual simplicity of the algorithm
  
  I'll likely need your advice about # 2. In your opinion, what orders of magnitude of "encoding latency" would be acceptable? Just to give some concrete context:
  - When I did some benchmarking, the early results suggested that this KEP wins 25k -> 60k and _improves_ "encoding latency" (measured for 40k nodes for fairness) from ~2ms to ~1.5ms.
  - Then, a "smarter" method reached ~130k for a few providers incl. AWS - but with latency ~45ms.
  - I also had an "even smarter" method reaching ~160k but that took ~300ms. \
    (So that in my feeling was way too slow - but I didn't know for sure)
  - To give you a feeling of "what's the ceiling", GZIPping the current format & storing it in base64 fits ~215k nodes, and took ~20ms. \
    (To be clear; I'm _not proposing_ to GZIP; this was just a mental experiment to convince ourselves that we shouldn't hope for fitting >200k nodes without additional CRDs).
  - Disclaimer: I am aware that Kueue will run on various hardware so such "absolute benchmarking" on my machine is skewing reality. (Though OTOH I'm feeling it's still better to discuss these numbers than have no numbers at all).

+  // +optional

```

  Thank you for checking that. In that case, it would be better to represent such mutually exclusive restrictions by API structuring. I think we can consider a well-known pattern, `union` / `discrimination union`, like the following.
  
  However, I think that the discrimination union looks overkill in this API. So, I would vote union pattern.
  The `individuals` might be better than `uniques` technically.
  
  - discrimination union
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    ...
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - prefix: pool-1-node-
         roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
         podCount:
           mode: universal | unique <- discriminator
           universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive against `uniques`
           uniques: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive against `universal`
  ```
  
  - union
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    ...
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - prefix: pool-1-node-
         roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
         podCount:
           universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive against `uniques`
           uniques: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive against `universal`
  ```
  
  UPDATED: I fixed some API field name typos for individuals and uniques.

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2025-11-07T22:56:27Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:998** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-11-07T22:56:27Z
```diff
@@ -904,29 +902,180 @@ type TopologyDomainAssignment struct {
 }
 ```
 
-Kueue uses the `kueue.x-k8s.io/topology` scheduling gate to delay the
-`nodeSelector` assignment, because different pods in the same PodSet may have
-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
```

  I see the point, and I mostly like it.
  (I'm a bit concerned that it'll make this API even more verbose - but, hopefully, still a bit clearer).
  
  But then, we'd need the same for "domain names". Let me check if I get that right:
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    ...
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
          prefix: pool-
          roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCount:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
  
  And then, I do feel one glitch in it. `individual` values, and inside them a `prefix` that is actually *not* individual, but applying to *all* these values... Wouldn't that be confusing?
  
  So maybe now saying `commonPrefix` / `commonSuffix` could help? Because now, I'm feeling that "the scope of over what it is common" will be defined well by the API structure.
  
  WDYT?

  Just to make it clear, I'm ok old API and with the new netested: 
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
          prefix: pool-
          roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCount:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
  If we go with nested I would just want to choose this approach both for valuesPerLevel and PodCount.
  
  I like `individual` more than `uniques` - it reads better. I don't see a substantial difference between `prefix` and `commonPrefix`  - I'm ok with both.

+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
```

  https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/7419#discussion_r2518609846
  
  This totally makes sense. But I proposed a slightly different API surface in the following:
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
         individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
           prefix: pool-
           roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCount:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individuals`
        individuals: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
  
  The different points are 1. `.topologyAssignment.slices[*].podCount` and 2. `.topologyAssignment.slices[*].individuals`.
  
  1: The reason for `podCount` instead of `podCounts` is that this field has a single podCount as opposed to multiple ones. Semantically, the multiply indicates that there are a number of pod count. But, the podCount has only one podCount since `universal` and `individuals` are mutually exclusive.
  2. The resson for `individuals` instead of `individual` is that the field serves a set of individual pod count.

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-11-14T20:43:43Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1094** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-11-14T20:43:43Z
```diff
@@ -904,29 +902,180 @@ type TopologyDomainAssignment struct {
 }
 ```
 
-Kueue uses the `kueue.x-k8s.io/topology` scheduling gate to delay the
-`nodeSelector` assignment, because different pods in the same PodSet may have
-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+}
+
+type TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues struct {
+  // commonPrefix specifies a common prefix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonPrefix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+  // commonSuffix specifies a common suffix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonSuffix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // roots specifies the values in this assignment, excluding commonPrefix and commonSuffix, if non-empty.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field of the TopologyAssignmentSlice.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Roots []string
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the topology assignment value (on the current topology level)
+  // that applies to every domain in the current slice.
+  // Mutually exclusive with roots, commonPrefix and commonSuffix.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalValue *string
+}
 ```
 
+The above mentioned cross-validity rules (mutually exclusive fields, equal lengths, etc.) will be all expressed as `kubebuilder:validation:XValidation` rules on the respective "smallest common container types".
+
+Example (representing the same assignment as in the first example for the [old format](#until-v1beta1)):
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  slices:
+  - size: 2
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - universalValue: block-1
+    - commonPrefix: rack-
+      roots: [1, 2]
+    counts: [4, 2]
+```
+
+The above example has one slice, specifying 2 domains on 2 topology levels. On the block level, all domains take the same value (`block-1`), which allows using `universalValue`. On the rack level, the values diverge (`rack-1`) vs. (`rack-2`) but they still share a relatively long common prefix. The new representation allows deduplicating characters between these.
+
+Multiple slices may be used e.g. for a host-level assignment when the nodes being assigned are split into multiple "node pools". The following example illustrates this for an assignment of 12 pods on 12 nodes (1 per 1), where the nodes come from 2 pools (of size 5 and 7 respectively), with node names looking like `pool-X-node-Y`:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels: [kubernetes.io/hostname]
+  slices:
+  - size: 5
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-1-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
+    universalCount: 1
+  - size: 7
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-2-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7]
+    universalCount: 1
+```
+
+The main motivation behind the new format is the etcd size limit of 1.5MiB per single resource, which currently restricts the number of nodes that can participate in the assignment for a single workload. (For the v1beta1 format, and the real-life node naming schemes of main K8s vendors, the limit is around 20-30k). The new format helps addressing this problem in 2 time perspectives:
+
+- In the short term, it increases the number of nodes which can fit into 1 etcd entry.
+
+  - By just using a single slice, with extracting common prefix and suffix of all node names, our simulations (for some real-life node naming schemes) suggested a limit of around 60k nodes.
```

  > I'll likely need your advice about # 2. In your opinion, what orders of magnitude of "encoding latency" would be acceptable? Just to give some concrete context:
  
  Unfortunately, I don't have the exact expected encoding latency at this time. 
  I would identify the boundary in the real cluster situation. So, if you can share the performace from your customers and shared with us, that would be great after this enhancement is released.
  
  The only request for now is that we should avoid introducing a compile/encoding mechanism to the API as much as possible, since such a mechanism typically loses the decrativity.
  
  OTOH, the current proposed prefix / suffix sounds better since it has better balance between encoding latency performance and readability.

```

  Regarding # 2: TBH I missed the `s` in `individuals` in your proposal. Apologies.
  This feels a bit counter-intuitive to me - because `universal` sounds like an adjective, and `individuals` sounds like a plural noun, which makes the API a bit less self-consistent.
  But if you align with @mimowo on this, I'll send a follow-up PR to change that.
  
  ---
  
  Regarding # 1: Here I'm not following.
  
  > The reason for podCount instead of podCounts is that this field has a single podCount as opposed to multiple ones.
  
  In general, I disagree. As your example shows, `podCount(s)` could contain an array (e.g. `[1, 2, 3, 4, 5]`). And then, in my eyes, it's no longer true that it "has a single pod count".
  
  Essentially, I share the sentiment expressed above by @mimowo:
  
  > If we go with nested I would just want to choose this approach both for valuesPerLevel and PodCount.
  
  So I'd like the same singular/plural naming pattern for `valuesPerLevel` and for the pod count(s).
  And I think `valuesPerLevel` / `podCounts` is much clearer than the singular alternatives.

  > The only request for now is that we should avoid introducing a compile/encoding mechanism to the API as much as possible, since such a mechanism typically loses the decrativity.
  
  I need follow-up questions to make sure I understand:
  
  - "decrativity" - what does this mean? declarativity? decorativity? (in any case, I'd benefit from a longer explanation)
  - by "introducing (...) to the API", do you mean changes of the public type definitions (which are not planned beyond this PR), or also changes of the implementation behind the scenes?
  - by "compile/encoding mechanism", do you mean sth like "let's use multiple slices, each with its own common prefix & suffix", or sth like "let's GZIP this and encode in base64"? \
    (to make it clear: we have _no plans_ to introduce the latter, even though it would likely compress best)

+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
```

  > Regarding # 2
  Ah, that sounds reasonable. I assumed that we use the `individual` as a noun. But, if we assume it as an `adjective`, that totally makes sense. If we can find a better noun name instead of `universal`, we can use `individuals`. But, I have no good name...
  
  > Regarding # 1
  
  As I mentiond in reply for #2, I assumed that `indivisual` is noun. But, in case of assuming adjective, I'm ok with `podCounts` since `podCounts.individual` could be translated to the `individual pod counts`.
  
  So, the final API surface is the following:
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
         individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
           prefix: pool-
           roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCounts:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
  
  @olekzabl Please let me know if there is missing anythig else, thanks!

@@ -904,29 +902,180 @@ type TopologyDomainAssignment struct {
 }
 ```
 
-Kueue uses the `kueue.x-k8s.io/topology` scheduling gate to delay the
-`nodeSelector` assignment, because different pods in the same PodSet may have
-different values:
+Example:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  domains:
+  - values: [block-1, rack-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [block-1, rack-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+Here:
+- 4 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-1
+  ```
+- 2 Pods are to be scheduled on nodes matching the node selector:
+  ```
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-block: block-1
+  cloud.provider.com/topology-rack: rack-2
+  ```
+
+Below there is an equivalent of the above example, assuming that the Topology
+object defines `kubernetes.io/hostname` as the lowest level in topology.
+Hence we omit higher topology levels, since the hostname label
+is sufficient to uniquely identify a particular node.
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - kubernetes.io/hostname
+  domains:
+  - values: [hostname-1]
+    count: 4
+  - values: [hostname-2]
+    count: 2
+```
+
+##### Since v1beta2
+
+In v1beta2, the data format is reshaped, with the main goal of improving handling of huge workloads. The 3 main ideas here are:
+
+- splitting the whole assignment structure into slices,
+- broader use of "parallel lists" which should be "zipped together" to produce their meaning \
+  (just like a _single_ list `Levels` in the old format specified the topology levels used in _every_ domain of the assignment),
+- extracting common prefixes and suffixes of node names.
 
 ```golang
-const (
-  // TopologySchedulingGate is used to delay scheduling of a Pod until the
-  // nodeSelectors corresponding to the assigned topology domain are injected
-  // into the Pod.
-  TopologySchedulingGate = "kueue.x-k8s.io/topology"
+type TopologyAssignment struct {
+  // (same role & comments as in v1beta1)
+  Levels []string
 
-  // WorkloadAnnotation is an annotation set on the Job's PodTemplate to
-  // indicate the name of the admitted Workload corresponding to the Job. The
-  // annotation is set when starting the Job, and removed on stopping the Job.
-  WorkloadAnnotation = "kueue.x-k8s.io/workload"
+  // slices represent topology assignments for subsets of pods of a workload.
+  // The full assignment is obtained as a union of all slices.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=30000
+  Slices []TopologyAssignmentSlice
+}
 
-  // TASLabel is a label set on the Job's PodTemplate to indicate that the
-  // PodSet is admitted using TopologyAwareScheduling, and all Pods created
-  // from the Job's PodTemplate also have the label.
-  TASLabel = "kueue.x-k8s.io/tas"
-)
+// TopologyAssignmentSlice fully specifies the topology assignment for a subset of pods of a workload.
+type TopologyAssignmentSlice struct {
+  // size is the number of domains covered by this slice.
+  // +required
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:Minimum=1
+  Size int32
+
+  // valuesPerLevel has one entry for each of the Levels specified in the TopologyAssignment.
+  // The entry corresponding to a particular level specifies the placement of pods at that level.
+  // +required
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=16
+  ValuesPerLevel []TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues
+
+  // counts specifies the number of pods allocated per each domain.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Counts []int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the number of pods allocated in every domain in this slice.
+  // Exactly one of count, universalCount must be set.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalCount *int32 `json:"omitempty"`
+}
+
+type TopologyAssignmentSliceLevelValues struct {
+  // commonPrefix specifies a common prefix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonPrefix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+  // commonSuffix specifies a common suffix for all values in this slice assignment.
+  // +optional
+  CommonSuffix *string `json:"omitempty"`
+
+  // roots specifies the values in this assignment, excluding commonPrefix and commonSuffix, if non-empty.
+  // May be omitted if all values are identical; if so, UniversalCount is used instead.
+  // If set, its length must be equal to the "size" field of the TopologyAssignmentSlice.
+  // +optional
+  // +listType=atomic
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=100000
+  Roots []string
+
+  // universalCount, if set, specifies the topology assignment value (on the current topology level)
+  // that applies to every domain in the current slice.
+  // Mutually exclusive with roots, commonPrefix and commonSuffix.
+  // +optional
+  UniversalValue *string
+}
 ```
 
+The above mentioned cross-validity rules (mutually exclusive fields, equal lengths, etc.) will be all expressed as `kubebuilder:validation:XValidation` rules on the respective "smallest common container types".
+
+Example (representing the same assignment as in the first example for the [old format](#until-v1beta1)):
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels:
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-block
+  - cloud.provider.com/topology-rack
+  slices:
+  - size: 2
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - universalValue: block-1
+    - commonPrefix: rack-
+      roots: [1, 2]
+    counts: [4, 2]
+```
+
+The above example has one slice, specifying 2 domains on 2 topology levels. On the block level, all domains take the same value (`block-1`), which allows using `universalValue`. On the rack level, the values diverge (`rack-1`) vs. (`rack-2`) but they still share a relatively long common prefix. The new representation allows deduplicating characters between these.
+
+Multiple slices may be used e.g. for a host-level assignment when the nodes being assigned are split into multiple "node pools". The following example illustrates this for an assignment of 12 pods on 12 nodes (1 per 1), where the nodes come from 2 pools (of size 5 and 7 respectively), with node names looking like `pool-X-node-Y`:
+
+```yaml
+topologyAssignment:
+  levels: [kubernetes.io/hostname]
+  slices:
+  - size: 5
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-1-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
+    universalCount: 1
+  - size: 7
+    valuesPerLevel:
+    - commonPrefix: pool-2-node-
+      roots: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7]
+    universalCount: 1
+```
+
+The main motivation behind the new format is the etcd size limit of 1.5MiB per single resource, which currently restricts the number of nodes that can participate in the assignment for a single workload. (For the v1beta1 format, and the real-life node naming schemes of main K8s vendors, the limit is around 20-30k). The new format helps addressing this problem in 2 time perspectives:
+
+- In the short term, it increases the number of nodes which can fit into 1 etcd entry.
+
+  - By just using a single slice, with extracting common prefix and suffix of all node names, our simulations (for some real-life node naming schemes) suggested a limit of around 60k nodes.
```

  > "decrativity" - what does this mean? declarativity? decorativity? (in any case, I'd benefit from a longer explanation)
  
  Sorry for your confusions. I meant `declarativity`.
  Yes, basically, I agree with the current prefix / suffix mechanism.
  
  > by "introducing (...) to the API", do you mean changes of the public type definitions (which are not planned beyond this PR), or also changes of the implementation behind the scenes?
  
  > by "introducing (...) to the API", do you mean changes of the public type definitions (which are not planned beyond this PR), or also changes of the implementation behind the scenes?
  
  I meant that the current mechanism and API surfaces looks good to me. No need to change at this cycle.
  
  > by "compile/encoding mechanism", do you mean sth like "let's use multiple slices, each with its own common prefix & suffix", or sth like "let's GZIP this and encode in base64"?
  (to make it clear: we have no plans to introduce the latter, even though it would likely compress best)

  > TBH, there's one more little divergence (mentioned somewhere above but we recently lost it from sight):
  I brought back common - because individual.prefix would sound weird for a prefix that is actually not individual.
  
  Yes, I still think that `common` does not represent the objective for the prefix.
  So, I still would like to propose `prefix` or `valuePrefix`.  Alternatively, we might be able to have more nested structure for roots. But, nested root fields sounds over-kill.
  
  If you want to represnet the objective for prefix, we can select `valuePrefix`. Please let me know which field name are you prefer.
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
          prefix: pool-
          roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCounts:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
  
  ```yaml
  topologyAssignment:
    slices:
    - valuesPerLevel:
      - universal: pool-1               <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual:                     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
          valuePrefix: pool-
          roots: [1, 1, 1, 2, 2]
      podCounts:
        universal: 2                    <- mutually exclusive with `individual`
        individual: [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]     <- mutually exclusive with `universal`
  ```
